“Hmm so what? You just don’t… date? No sneaky hookups with curious housewives?” Rio asked with another smirk.



“Nope, if there are any curious housewives here they most certainly aren’t hooking up with me. But I prefer it, I have Nicky every other week and the drama club when the school isn’t closed, that keeps me busy pretty much all the time, and I guess one muddies the pool when you’ve already divorced one of only two available lesbians in town, plus she’s technically dating the other one.”



“Wow, that sounds… bleak.” Rio said, pulling her face.



“Why do you want to know?” Agatha asked casually.



“Well you never know when you might meet a curious housewife…” she said with a wink. 



Before Agatha could respond to that ridiculous answer there was a knock on the front door. “That’s probably Alice.”



Rio greeted Alice with a wave and a smile when she walked in, “I’ll give you two some space. I will be back in an hour, I think I will go check out the coffee shop you mentioned.” 



“Uhm, okay. I guess I’ll see you later.” She replied.



Rio smiled at her and stepped outside and Agatha almost felt the air in the house shift. She stared at the closed door for a moment when Alice pulled her back to reality.



“You two seem comfortable…” Alice said when Rio pulled the door shut as she walked out.



“Don’t start Al…” Agatha warned.



Rio’s POV 



Rio pulled the front door closed, walked to her car and climbed in to drive to the town center. She made small mental notes while she listened as Agatha listed the limited number of things to do in town. She wanted to take her on a date, the one she meant to plan before Agnes disappeared. 



She pulled her car into a parking space on the side of the street. Small shop fronts lined the street on both sides. A florist, some strange boutique clothing shop with hideous floral dresses in the window, a thrift shop selling something of everything and a small coffee shop, Wiccan Brew and Books. She’ll start there.



Rio approached the counter and placed an order for an iced coffee with the teenager behind the register.



“You’re not from here.” The teenager said. Rio noticed his eyeliner and pierced ears. He looked out of place in this seemingly plain town.



“What gave it away, kid?” She asked.



“There are only two other people in town who normally order this in November, me and this edgy cop… And now you. People here are more of the cappuccino or flat white types. Especially when it’s cold.” He said, lifting an amused brow.



“I think you could say I am visiting an old friend.” Rio paused, taking in the kid standing in front of her. “So I guess this means you know most people here, huh?”



He paused his movements, dropping his hand holding the coffee grounds on the counter, “Depends who’s asking.” He said, clearly trying to sum her up in some way.



Rio laughed softly, “Look I am not here to make any trouble. Just curious. I am not used to small town living. I barely know my neighbor, and this place feels different. Like everyone knows everyone’s business you know.”



“When you work in the only coffee shop in Westview, you tend to get to know people by their coffee orders. Like take Mrs. Davis, my high school drama teacher, always orders the sweetest drink on the menu, her teeth are probably rotting already, but it sort of suits her because she is almost insufferably sweet in person. It’s annoying really. Then there is Mr. Harris, always angry, always a double shot black coffee...”



Rio felt her eyes glass over, “Okay so you do know almost everyone’s business. And you go to Westview High, I assume.”



“Yes unfortunately, but I am graduating next year, and then I am out of here. This town feels more like a waiting room, if you know what I mean.” He said winking.



“So you are part of our soccer team then?” Rio said, more to herself than anything else.



“I don’t know what that means.” He said confused.



“Don’t worry about it. So where would be a good place for a date?” Rio saw the boy’s eyes stretch open, “Not with you dummy, with Ag… with my friend.”



Rio saw the realization in his face. Fuck, her and her big mouth, she thought. 



“Oh, so you’re old friend is Ms. Harkness. Dirty Chai, double shot, with sugar if she looks like she’s had a bad day, which is usually a lot this time of the year.”



Usually a lot this time of the year… this time of year was when her life was thrown upside down. 



“How do you know Ms. Harkness?” He asked, handing her her order.



Rio took a seat behind the counter. “We knew each other… back in college.” Rio realized she actually didn’t know anything about Agnes, let alone Agatha. 



“She’s my favorite teacher. I don't even like history, but she always lets me sit in her class on off periods, and she was married to my science teacher but that was before I was in high school. They still come here together though, with their son Nicky, and Ms. Hill’s girlfriend. It’s nice that they are still friends...”



“We’re getting sidetracked here,” Rio realized she met the most talkative person in Westview.



“Oh right, the date.” He smiled.



“Yeah, although I am already regretting asking. You’re probably going to blab everything to her before I even get to actually ask her.”



“Promise I won’t, I’m great at keeping secrets. Ok so here’s the deal, this place,” he swirled his hand in the air, “not really date worthy. But if you’re willing to add a twenty minute drive to your date, the next town over, Eastview, I know, real original with the names… it has this amazing Korean barbecue place and right across from the street they have a haunted house that does ghost tours, it’s really fun and Ms. Harkness would love it because it's like historical or something.”



“That actually sounds perfect, kid. Don’t tell her I asked you. I will deny it and blame you for being a creep.” Rio warned sucking up the last bit of her drink. She put down the plastic cup, hopped off the chair and walked out. “Thanks Teen!” 



Rio walked out of the coffee shop, the idea actually really sounded good. Ghost tour followed by a nice dinner. Weird enough to be fun. She walked to the florist and bought a small bouquet of assorted purple flowers before getting back in her car to drive back to Agatha’s. Hopefully her and Alice’s talk was over, she didn’t want to be in the way. 



Pulling up in Agatha’s driveway, she saw Alice’s car still parked in front of the garage. She hadn’t really been gone longer than an hour, maybe she should have stayed away longer, she thought. Unsure of what exactly to expect, she left the bunch of flowers in the car and got out. She carefully walked up to the front door and hesitated for a second before opening the door.



When she entered the living room she saw Agatha crying with her head in her hands and Alice sitting next to her obviously trying to console her. Agatha’s head shot up and Rio briefly met her eyes. “I uhm, I’ll come back later…” she turned around as quick as she came in and went to sit in her car. 



What the fuck was happening in there…

Nobody Said It Was Easy

Chapter Summary

Agatha is STRESSED folks... But Rio might just be a necessary distraction.

Chapter Notes

Wanted to post this last week but my wife surprised me with an anniversary weekend away and no, the laptop stayed home...

Agatha’s POV



“I’ll give you two some space. Agatha, I will be back in an hour, I think I will go check out the coffee shop you mentioned.” 



“Uhm, okay. I guess I’ll see you later.” She replied. Rio probably could have stayed but Agatha appreciated the privacy, in case things got too much. She didn’t really know Rio, so keeping some things under wraps for now seemed reasonable.



“You two seem comfortable…” Alice said with her mischievous smile.



“Don’t start Al…” Agatha warned. “She slept in the guest room, that's all. Westview only has that creepy motel, so other than her car, she didn’t really have any other option.”



“I was simply making an observation. You are way too defensive this morning.” 



“Sit, I need more coffee.” Agatha poured two cups and walked back to the living room. She gave Alice her cup and sat down on the sofa. 



“So what do I do now? Two people from my past life suddenly showing up out of nowhere… I was supposed to disappear. If they found me this easily without even trying too hard, how easily would Ralph’s guys find me if they actually tried? The stakes are so much higher than it was then. What if they found me, and Nicky?” Agatha felt herself spiraling.



“Well technically I brought Jen to you and she told Rio. So as it stands now, no one was actively looking for you. And the guys in the program have alerts on any movement of known associates of RB. If they were looking, we would have known about it already.”



Agatha looked at Alice. Was she overreacting? “It’s been ten years, Alice. Is that long enough for them to forget about me? To stop looking?”



“Look, I can ask around. If it will make you feel better. There is this guy in the agency who has contacts in the prison system who can dig without making noise. They will be able to find out if RB’s guys have been looking for you.”



Agatha sighed. This wasn’t a sure answer but Alice would tell her if there was anything. “What do you know about my mother? Jen said she disappeared as well.”



Alice stayed quiet, almost too long. “Alice? What do you know?”



“Look I don’t really know much, okay. To keep you safe I am only told what I need to know and apparently I don’t need to know anything about that.”



“So you do know something, I know when you lie to me Alice. You have a clear tell.” Agatha said.



“I don’t,” Alice said defensively.



“Alice, you pull on your left ear every time. How do you think I always beat you in poker?” Agatha pulled her own ear to show Alice.



Alice immediately grabbed her ears. “Fine, I know something but I am technically not supposed to. And if I’m technically not supposed to know, you are definitely not supposed to know. Urgh I am actually such a bad cop.” 



“It’s not that bad, Alice. You just think you are way more badass than you actually are.” Agatha laughed.



Alice rolled her eyes, “Whatever, it’s a fake job anyway, keeping your ass safe is my actual job and so far I’m doing great.”



“You were the one who blew my cover first… If I didn’t like having you around instead of some other babysitter… I didn’t even know you were dating. You almost hid her better than you are hiding me…” Agatha’s thoughts drifted back to the mess she was in now. “But seriously Alice, what do you know?”



“The trial exposed a lot of ethics violations. Her law firm partner, Lilia, had a lot of fires to put out. Some criminal cases had to be retried, bad people got off that really shouldn’t have and innocent people were sitting in prison because of her… She was bad news. I actually don’t know how you two are related... The last thing I heard, and the last thing I am willing to tell you now, was that she was living under a fake name somewhere and working for some sketchy guys on the west coast as their defense lawyer, they had eyes on her but other than identity theft and generally being a shitty person, they don’t have enough to prosecute her for anything else.”



“I knew growing up that she wasn’t a good person, she could never hide that completely. Lilia felt more like my mother, she actually loved me and cared for me. Evanora was like an evil stepmother.” Agatha missed Lilia so much. “I sometimes wished Lilia was my real mother…”



“She sounds like a good person to have around.” Alice said apologetically.



The room fell quiet. Agatha stared at the guest room door where Rio stood in her t-shirt this morning. A small smile crept on her face. “I sometimes wish a lot of things never happened.” she said to no one. 



“Agatha, you had to rebuild everything in your life. That isn’t an easy thing to do. When I first met you, you were the saddest person I’ve ever seen. You were crying all the time and I practically had to drag your ass into the shower some days. Look at what you made for yourself. You have this amazing home, a job you actually love, an amazing kid, and me. You are strong Agatha, you are resilient and so brave. Whatever happens with RB, we will deal with it. But I promise you the same thing I did ten years ago. I will do my best to keep you safe, you need to trust me, okay.”



Agatha started crying. It was the fear of the unknown, her past life creeping back into her present, her missing Lilia and even Wanda, it was everything she had bottled up spilling over again. Alice jumped up and ran to her side to console her. 



“Agatha, I promise okay.” Alice said, rubbing Agatha’s back. 



“I’m a mess, Alice. I know it doesn’t always look like it, but I am. And now Rio is here and I have no fucking idea what I am doing. I kissed her last night. I didn’t even say hello or nice to see you , I just kissed her out of nowhere.”



“I thought there was a vibe. You never said anything about her when we met.” Alice said curiously.



“We were never really anything, we barely spent five hours together at a friend’s Halloween party, we had ice cream at 1am and then she made sure I got home safe, I told her I’d text her and that was the last time I saw her before this all happened. Till she showed up here. Now I am so confused, it feels like it was just yesterday, but so much time has passed since that night. I am literally a different person now. But I always felt we were… unfinished. We never got the chance to even try to be anything. And now… now she is here…what the fuck does that even mean? What is she doing here?” Agatha felt the tears burning in her eyes as she cried into her hands. 



She heard movement in front of her and when she looked up, there Rio was standing. What did she actually hear? But before Agatha could comprehend anything, Rio ran out the door. 



“Fuck,” Agatha said, sniffing as she wiped the tears from her face. “Do you think…” 



“No, she just came in, she couldn’t have heard anything. But Agatha, you need to talk to her. I know things are a mess now, but you’ll feel better. I highly doubt there was any physical traceable link between you and Rio before all this, so there will be no lead to you from her unless she talks directly to RB or his guys. And from what I have heard about her from Jen, she seems fiercely loyal to those close to her. She should be fine.”



“Yeah, are you sure? I don’t want to pull her into something that she would be safer without, you know.” Agatha said concerned.



“I’m sure Agatha, but if you need me too, I could… look into her. See who she is to be safe.” Alice suggested.



“No, please don’t. I don’t want to invade her personal life. I feel like I can trust her.”



Alice stood up and grabbed her bag. “Agatha, please don’t worry too much. Let me see what I can find out about RB before we stress too much and overthink this.”



“Thank you Alice.” Agatha hugged her and walked to the door with her. She opened the front door and immediately saw Rio sitting in her car. She laughed and after Alice left she walked over to the driver’s side of the car and knocked. Rio let down the window.



“Hi,” Agatha said sheepishly.



Rio bit her bottom lip, “Hey,” she replied awkwardly.



Agatha took a step back and gestured to the house. “It’s safe to come inside if you want” She waited for Rio to open the car door and get out. “I need actual food so I’m going to warm up a mac and cheese for lunch.”



“You barely know me, but you already know what I love to eat.” Rio said as she climbed out of the car and followed Agatha inside the house.



Rio’s POV



Rio followed Agatha to the kitchen where Agatha took out a frozen meal from the freezer and turned on the oven to warm it up. When she sat down behind the kitchen counter she realised she forgot the flowers in the car. Agatha felt too quiet. Was she always this quiet or did the talk with Alice upset her too much to talk to her.

Rio stared at the message. Somehow she felt it too. She’s always missed something or someone and now she knew. It was her she missed.

Rio fell back onto her pillows and stared up at the ceiling. She smiled and turned to her side looking at the moon through her curtains, picturing Agatha’s blue eyes looking back at her and eventually falling asleep.

Navy Blue

Chapter Notes

I am overwhelmed with the response this is getting, thank you!

Agatha’s POV



Agatha sat at her desk in her classroom. She had a free period before the next class would start, so she continued with the last papers she still had left to grade. The weekend put her a bit behind schedule. She heard a knock on the door. Not looking up from the papers in front of her she answered, “Busy…”



“Hey Ags,” she heard Maria say. She looked up and saw her leaning against the doorframe.



“Maria, sorry. Come in.” Agatha said, taking off her glasses and putting them down on the stack of papers.



“Sorry for interrupting.” Maria walked to sit in one of the chairs in front of her desk. “Are you okay?”



Agatha sat back in her chair. Why wouldn’t she be? “Yeah? Why are you asking?”



“Nicky said you were weird when you spoke to him Saturday. Weirder than usual for this time of year.” Oh, the phone call. Nicky was always intuitive and must have picked up on something. 



Agatha remembered the part of her backstory explaining her being weird this time of year. She wanted to relocate after her estranged parents suddenly died. Vague enough to make it believable and also to explain why she didn’t have any family members to invite to their wedding.



“Oh…” Agatha replied quietly. “Yeah. Sorry, I didn’t mean to be weird.” 



“You can tell me if something is wrong, you know. We are… friends.” Maria said smiling. 



Agatha always loved that about Maria. Even though their marriage never worked out, Maria was still a good friend, understanding and caring. Agatha put her through hell, and Maria never held that against her.



“I’m fine really. I had a bit too much to drink Friday night and I had a hell of a hangover.”



“I heard I missed a big show at Tony’s.” Maria teased.



Agatha covered her face in embarrassment. “Oh god, I told Jen and Al to keep me away from the karaoke machine.”



“Jen?” Maria asked.



Shit… “Uh yeah, Al’s new girlfriend.” Agatha tried to correct herself.



“I didn’t know she was dating. I don’t know why, but I thought you two were secretly a thing…”



“Me and Alice?” Agatha laughed. “Never happening.”

Billy appeared at the door, peeking his head through the door. 



“I thought that other cool mystery woman was going to ask you out, Ms. H.” he interrupted.



“Billy,” Agatha said, her eyes almost popping out of her head. 



Maria looked at Agatha and stood up walking towards the door again. “Well, I guess I was wrong about a lot of things. Anyway Ags, come to dinner tonight, I’m making your favorite and Nicky would love to see you.”

She was serious and a straight to the point kind of person and Agatha respected that, she always knew where she stood with her and she also appreciated that she treated Maria and Nicky so well. “Because, you don’t have one.” Maria teased.

“I sort of already knew her, from college so no, not a complete stranger… but let’s talk about something else. My love life can’t be the only hot topic of the night…”

Somehow Agatha was everywhere she looked and everything she thought of.

The moment she stepped off the treadmill and caught her breath, a vision of Agatha’s smile popped back in her head. Frustrated, Rio threw her hand towel over her face and paced back and forth. “Get it together Vidal!” she grumbled to herself.



Stepping into the bathroom Rio turned on the warm water to a scolding heat. The room filled with steam as the hot water poured over her body, stinging just enough to give her the necessary effect. 



After she’d cleaned herself and dried off she slipped into her pajamas and fell onto the bed in a huff, her phone held over her face with her chats open. Her fingers hovered over Agatha’s name and after considering and reconsidering she tapped on her name and typed a message.



Rio: How is Westview’s favorite teacher doing?



No response.

She stared out of the kitchen window looking over the city lights stretched out before her. Finishing the last sip she sauntered back. Agatha: I’ll have to ask Ms. Davis.



Rio: Please, I am sure she’s got nothing on you. Unless she’s got some GILF action going…

Rio: A date? 



Agatha: If you wanted to. 



Rio: I would love that.



Rio was grinning to herself, she felt giddy, excited. She had no idea when she would be able to see her again, but the prospect of it was enough for now.



Rio: I can’t wait.



Agatha’s POV



Agatha laid in bed, the wine from dinner at Maria’s was mulling around in her head. She sighed as she read Rio’s last message “I can’t wait” over and over again. Despite all the crap going on around her she was happy to have reconnected with Rio, and even with Jen. All potential danger aside, it was good to think she had some part of her old life with her now. Something to keep her from feeling like a stranger in her own life.



She couldn’t remember the last time she felt this optimistic or hopeful about anything really. To the people around her, she came across as fine, content even, but inside she always felt like a big imposter. She knew some days her smile didn’t reach her eyes, her sunglasses hid them most days. Her laughter had been forced here and there, the quality of the conversations aside, she didn’t find a lot of things to laugh about. 



Happiness wasn’t something that always came naturally to her in Westview. Not since that night anyway. But she has had happy moments since then, if she was honest with herself. Her wedding day with Maria was a happy day. Or at least, she felt happy. And Nicky’s birth was difficult, but she remembers feeling happiness as she held him for the first time. Seeing him grow up also brought many happy moments. 



Now after the weekend she felt terrified but… happy. Maybe the wine helped, and seeing Nicky, but no one could explain how she felt now, not even Agatha herself.



She typed one last message to Rio.



Agatha: I am really happy to have met you… again. Sleep well Rio. 



She didn’t wait for a reply, simply turned onto her side after locking her phone and fell into a peaceful sleep.

Here We Go Again

Chapter Summary

Project Darkhold kicks off

Rio’s POV

Today’s plan was reconnaissance with Lilia. She still needed to find a good enough reason to suddenly want to know where Agnes went, they weren’t friends before that Halloween night. That’s why Jen was coming here. She had a perfect reason to ask. They were friends and roommates. Understandable and plausible.

Busted, Rio thought. Even a bad lawyer would have asked that same question.

Rio: Please ignore this if it is too sappy, but I just wanted you to know that I was thinking of you.

Hide and Seek

Chapter Summary

Yay, a reunion!

Agatha’s POV



Friday finally came as a relief to Agatha. The school play had her busy every night until late. She missed Nicky, who she was picking up Sunday morning, and somewhat surprisingly, she missed Rio. Alice has also been missing during the week, which wasn’t as strange to Agatha, since Alice was one of a few police officers in their small town. 



Agatha sat in her car exhausted from finally finishing the last rehearsal of the week with the drama club. She looked at the clock on her dashboard, 19:25. To her relief, they actually finished at a decent time today, meaning she could still meet Alice for dinner before getting into bed early for the first night in a week.



She sent a confirmation text to Alice to meet at Tony’s and turned the car on.



At Tony’s she pulled into an open parking space and just as she was about to get out, she heard her phone ring. It was Rio.



“Rio?” Agatha answered surprised.



“Hey, uh Agatha, how are you?” Rio greeted.



“I’m good,” Agatha heard what sounded like a big party in the background, “Rio, where are you?”



Rio let out a laugh. “Look up.” she heard Rio say. 



“What?” Agatha asked, confused.



“I said, look… up.”



Still confused, Agatha frowned and shook her head as she obeyed and looked up over her steering wheel, and standing there in the two spotlights of her car’s headlights, there was Rio, waving at her with a smirk on her face.

Chapter Summary

Salemite: I know I have you by the throat, Old Hag. I trust you’ll know keeping this from me will not be in your best interest.

Q

Chapter Summary

Who is Q?

Chapter Notes

Well fuck, AAA week was a blast! There are sooooo many talented writers on here!

I hit a bit of a block TBH, but I am back. Inspiration has struck and as an apology y'all are getting a double post today!

The prison system for young girls was brutal, but for a 14 year old delinquent it meant a bed and a warm meal every day, not that she would ever call the slop they served in the dining hall a warm meal . At least it was more than she was accustomed to at home. 



Qiaolian grew up in a small apartment in the slums of Beijing with her parents and sister. They had very little and had even less to look forward to other than hoping to get a decent paying job in the city after finishing school or to somehow leave China in pursuit of greener pastures. Her parents worked in the service industry. Her father was a custodian at their school and her mother worked as a cleaning lady at a run down hotel close to their home. 



Despite working their asses off, they barely made ends meet and getting food on the table became a daily struggle. When Qiaolain was old enough to understand their dire situation, she decided to do whatever she could to help her parents and eventually resorted to petty crimes, stealing food, clothes and other goods to sell to help pay the rent for their shoddy one bedroom apartment.



She wasn’t the only kid in town fighting for the survival of her family, and eventually that resulted in her falling into some very unsavory crowds. One night while trying to get what she needed for her family, she ended up being part of a small group of teenagers trying to hijack and rob a delivery truck and that was how she ended up in debt with the Cobalt Serpents. Before she knew it she was initiated and part of the dangerous gang. Drugs, weapons, you name it, anything was trade and everything had a price, be it in dollars or in lives.



She actually managed to survive the first two years as part of the gang without being caught by the authorities and the extra income she managed to get for her family was more than welcome. She explained the sudden influx of spare cash and food as getting a job at a grocer, keeping her involvement with the gang a secret from her family. 



It was on one of the gang’s latest seedy operations where she ended up being caught and thrown in prison with the other members who worked with her that night. Their mission to move a gross amount of heroin went horribly wrong. She watched her best friend violently get shot and others injured and barely escaped injury herself. Unfortunately she was caught, tried and thrown in jail until her 18th birthday. 



Walking out of the gates of the prison a dark van was waiting for her and the rest of her life was determined just then. The freedom she dreamt she could have after spending two years behind bars in horrible conditions, was just that, a pipedream. Instead she fell right back into the gang’s claws, this time older and experienced , she was taken under the wing of the big boss of the Serpents, Shétóu a.k.a. Snake Head. 



Like the meaning of his name he was the ruthless leader of the Serpents. He was a man of power and influence, hiding in plain sight as the head of a rehabilitation center for young women exciting the prison system. Under his guise, he took in and trained the young women to be spies and assassins for hire. With her included they were a total of at least fifteen girls living in the compound being trained and eventually sent off to wherever they were needed, scattered across the world on their own missions.



She was happy at the compound. She made new friends and grew stronger every day. Her new life came with an excellent education and even better training in combat and black ops. When she was ready, she got her first orders and was shipped off to a new country on her first official solo mission.



For the next few months she settled into her new undercover persona. Now known as Gina, she worked in a local hardware store, waiting for her target to be close enough to take out. Admittedly, she lived comfortably. She had a small cozy apartment and enjoyed her quiet life in the small German town she now called home. Her old life as Qiaolain, completely forgotten.



All things considered, she was lonely. Something she never really had was real love, and a life with the Serpents didn’t make that any easier to get. When she was back in town after finally tracking down and eliminating her target in the town next over, she took a well deserved break, nursing a drink in the local bar of a small German town. There she met and eventually fell in love with Lisa, a local woman who stole her heart and let her believe that a simple life outside of the Serpents could be possible. Suddenly she found herself wanting to rather build a future with this woman instead of the life of crime she had come accustomed to.



One call on her burner phone, letting her know of her next mission and target, changed everything. After the call ended she made the impulsive decision of tossing the phone into the river below her, and ultimately running away with her new girlfriend, eventually settling in a small rural town across the border where they settled in a cozy apartment with their two cats. For almost a year, life felt good and she was finally free. Or so she thought.  



Late one night after a long day’s work, she walked home to their apartment. It was snowing gently around her and the smell of mulled wine hung in the air. Opening the front door to the apartment, she fell to her knees. Her heart broke as she cried out in physical pain. Unfortunately, this was a scene she wasn’t a stranger to. She has left worse herself, but those people were faceless. This time, the face staring blankly up at her in a pool of blood was that of her first love, Lisa. And next to her bloody body, a note.



Once a Serpent, always a Serpent.     



They found her and just like that, she was back in the claws of the Serpents. That was how she found herself living in the USA. Back to her life as a paid assassin in the grips of the life she desperately tried to escape, only this time her mission included a family and friends and a little boy who she tried her best to ignore and not love. 



She thought she had turned cold after losing Lisa, leading her to believe she would be capable of staying cold and unaffected by those around her. So when her old handler approached her for her new mission, she had no reason not to agree to infiltrate the small town of Westview as Melinda May, to befriend a stranger, keep her close and eventually turn her in when the time came.

She always imagined her punishment would be brutal for all the violence and murder that littered her past but this was a punishment worse than she had ever imagined. Now she had no idea how to get out of this mess.

Failing her mission meant the death of her girlfriend Maria and her son Nicky. This was worse than collateral. This was her family now, who she really loved. In the corner, a worn brown sofa stood next to small coffee table with a glass of water and a plate of what looked like a dried up sandwich.



This was a weird fucking dream, Agatha thought to herself. Only this wasn’t a dream, because if it were her head would not be throbbing the way it was now. Agatha moved to get up from the floor and to see if she could look out of the small window of the room. Her legs wobbled slightly under her weight but she managed to get up to the window in one piece.



She seemed to be in some sort of basement, she thought. From the small window she saw a shed and the back of a car she didn’t recognize. Agatha tried to open the window but it was locked or welded shut. “ Fuck!” she yelled out as she slumped against the wall and slid to the floor.



Immediately she remembered what day it was, Thanksgiving. Nicky’s favorite holiday, now definitely ruined forever. If she had just been strong enough to fight off her assailant. Agatha thought back to Dottie’s neighborhood watch self protection class Agatha was pulled into. At the time Agatha and Alice joined in reluctantly, laughing and making fun to get through the hour. She should have taken it way more seriously because look at the shitshow of a situation she was in now. Maybe the housewife karate would have been handy.



Agatha sat with her hands in her hair thinking and feeling the lump forming at the side where the asshole knocked her unconscious. If they were going to kill her, she would be dead already, her lifeless body would be lying in a pool of her own blood somewhere in the safehouse, but no, here she was, still alive. This didn’t make sense. They were keeping her alive for some reason. Ralph didn’t have any reason to keep her alive unless they needed her for something.



But for what and for how long?



A noise startled her coming from the door at the top of the basement stairs. Someone was unlocking it. Agatha got up and moved to the corner, looking around for anything to defend herself with. She grabbed the glass of water and held it tightly, she could smash the glass against the wall and use a shard of glass if needed. Stupid fucking idea, but the room was empty other than the smelly sofa and the old sandwich which did not look like something she would be eating any time soon.



The door creaked open and two sets of heavy shoes descended down the staircase. 



A man she didn’t recognize lead down the stairs and when Agatha lifted her eyes to the two people her heart dropped. Evanora.



“Mother. Fuck, of course.” Agatha spat, shaking her head. Her silent tears rolled down her face. No surprise that this fucking devil of a woman was behind all of it. “Long time no see.” 



“Don’t get smart with me Agnes. You know I don’t like that tone.” Evanora said harshly.



“You could have called.” Agatha smiled sarcastically.



“Let’s cut to the chase, sweetheart.” Evanora said. “You caused a lot of trouble with your statement, putting an innocent man in jail.”



Agatha laughed dryly, “Innocent? I saw him shoot and kill those men, mother. He was far from innocent.”



“You have always been a terrible liar my dear.” Evanora grinned. “And now the time has come for you to tell the truth. The whole truth, so help you God. For your sake and Agatha Harkness’ sake.”



“The truth? What is this?” Agatha watched as the man accompanying her mother set up a tripod with a camera attached on top in front of the sofa. 



“Your one and only chance, my dear. To tell the whole world the truth and to tell them what a dirty little liar you are. How you made up the whole story to get some much needed attention, you know, mommy or daddy issues, whomever you need to blame. You see, my old client was innocent, and because of your dirty mouth and obvious desperate need for attention, he has spent the last decade behind bars, atoning for someone else’s crimes.”



Agatha’s mouth hung open in awe. “You can’t be serious.” 



“Oh I am. Dead serious. The newly found evidence will show that everything was planted, and that you were coaxed into delivering a false statement, perjury is a punishable offence, dear. A felony in the state of Pennsylvania, and I am willing to ask the judge for the maximum sentence for a crime of this magnitude. What that poor man had to endure behind bars… you should be ashamed of yourself.”



“I won’t…” Agatha spat. 



“Oh you will, and you will make it very believable. I didn’t pay for those silly drama lessons for nothing. We both know can be quite the actress if you actually tried. You managed to keep up the act of Agatha Harkness for ten years didn’t you, the Oscars never saw you coming, my dear.”



“And if I don’t? What then? You’ll just kill me?” Agatha frowned.



“Oh no, never. I am not a murderer. I will however let you suffer your own consequences. Or should I say, let them suffer your consequences.”



“Them?” Agatha asked nervously.



“Nicholas Harkness. Rio Vidal. Ring a bell?” Evanora chuckled to herself. “To name a few.”



“You wouldn’t.” Agatha said, launching herself at her mother.



Evanora didn’t move an inch, “Oh, would you like to test me? We got to you pretty easily, despite the whole army marching around that old hag’s barn. Lilia was never a subtle woman. That house practically screamed safehouse. Now if you would be so kind as to join me on the sofa for your live apology.” 



******************



Rio’s POV



Sitting around and waiting for any news felt like waiting for the end of the world to come. Rio was restless and poor Nicky was inconsolable. The news of his mother’s kidnapping hit him like a punch to the gut. Luckily, he had a small army of loved ones around him to keep his spirits up.



Rio tried to distract him with more PlayStation game challenges, but her heart wasn’t in it. She felt paralyzed with guilt for not being able to get to her on time and the fear of never seeing her again was ripping a hole straight through her heart.



The amount of agents and officers in the house wasn’t helping either. It seemed everyone was looking busy but no results came of it. No one knew where to even start with tracking her down.



With the Thanksgiving dinner now forgotten, Rio and Nicky sat on the floor in the living room with the television’s sound turned down to a quiet murmur. Maria, sitting on the sofa near them, was attentively keeping an eye on the news bulletins as they came up, while Rio was teaching Nicky a card game to keep him distracted.



“Oh fuck,” Maria yelled out. Rio’s head snapped up immediately. “It’s her. It’s Agatha!”



Maria turned up the volume on the television as Alice and Lilia ran into the living room.



“We have received news of a live video feed sent to us via an encrypted source. This seems to be related to the missing Westview woman, Agatha Harkness, who disappeared from safe custody earlier this morning.” The talking head reported.



From where Rio was sitting, her eyes were instantly glued to the screen as she dropped the pack of cards, jumping up from her seat on the floor.



The news channel switched over to the live feed where a dim room came into frame. There she saw her. Agatha, sitting in front of a camera, wide eyed and nervous. 



“Mama!” Nicky yelled. 



“Nicky, come with me.” Maria said, pulling at his arm to take him out of the room. 



“But its…” Nicky cried.



“Nic, baby please. Let the police do their work. Come with me outside, I will explain everything later, okay?” Maria said, pulling him out of the view from the television.



Rio watched as Nicky reluctantly left with his other mother and turned back to the television. Agatha looked fine, well alive at least, but her eyes were red from obviously crying. Rio wished she could reach through the screen to grab her and never let her go.



After the camera in front of Agatha settled, she took a shaky breath. “My name is Ag… Agnes O’Connor, currently known as Agatha Harkness. I testified under oath in court that I witnessed a crime, a murder, ten years ago in Philadelphia.” 



Agatha dropped her head and ran her hands through her hair. Rio took a step closer to the television. “Is this… can they trace this…” she asked before turning back to the TV.



“My testimony…” Agatha continued, interrupting Rio’s questioning to the agents in the room. “My testimony resulted in the guilty verdict of Mr. Ralph Bohner.”



Rio felt the tears roll over her face as she saw Agatha visibly fighting every word coming out of her mouth.



“I am here today to…” she cleared her throat and shook her head, looking up at nothing to hide the fact that she was crying. “...to set the record straight that I… that I…” Agatha bit her lip and smiled a wicked teary smile. “...I was forced to confess… THAT I HAVE BEEN KIDNAPPED BY MY MOTHER AND I AM NOW BEING BLACKMAILED TO RETRACT…”



The screen went dark.  



“No, NO! ” Rio cried as the woman she loved with all her heart disappeared from the screen in front of her.



The dark screen flickered back to the news anchors. “Our producers have sent this footage and all other information to the authorities to help find the kidnapped woman…”



Alice turned off the television and the room went silent. 



“Alice. What do we do?” Rio asked, no, pleaded.



“This is good Rio, trust me.” Alice said, hugging her. “They need her and this shows they are desperate. We can work with this.”



Alice stood thinking for a second. “Lilia, your firm handled the RB case right?” 



“Yes, well Evanora did.” Lilia answered.



“What if we could bait them somehow? Fool them to think that we will give up something that might clear his name or something.” Alice asked, turning Lilia.



“Not after that ?” Rio interrupted them, “Not after what she just did… She just blew up their plan…”



“Evanora needs this, if she could clear his name somehow, it gets her off the hook too. We’ll have to be smart about this, Evanora is smart. She definitely has some judge in her pocket to be able to get the testimony thrown out.” Lilia spoke so surely, Rio almost felt relieved, but she couldn’t help the gnawing feeling that they were naive to think that they wouldn’t hurt Agatha.  



******************



Agatha’s POV



“That was fucking stupid,” Evanora snarled, slapping her cheek. “Did you think I was joking when I said I would get to them? Your family ?”



Agatha grabbed her face as it stung from her mother’s hand, she knew she fucked up by pulling that stunt, but she had to take the risk. She needed to fight, to get out of this alive and to get back to Nicky and Rio, but giving in to her mother was never going to happen.



“You rotten child.” Evanora spat, walking away frustratedly. 



“What are you going to do to me?” Agatha asked, taunting and genuinely curious. “I’m still your daughter, could you really be this cruel?”



“Cruel?” Evanora said sharply, “I gave you everything. You were too weak to rise up to any of my expectations. You could have been great, but you are just like your pathetic father.” 



“Just because I didn’t want to be a fucking shark like you, I am pathetic? Please mother…” Agatha huffed, “You seek power and cling on to anyone with money, no matter which side of right or wrong they are on. I may not be some big shot lawyer with a dirty conscience or an offshore bank account, but I have real friends and people who love me and care for me. Who do you have, mother?”



Agatha saw her mother seething at her words. She hit a nerve and that was as clear as day and she was now playing a dangerous game. She has never stood up to her mother, not like this, and especially not with someone else’s lives on the line.



Evanora let out a deep evil chuckle. “My girl, do you think I care about that? About you? You are greatly mistaken. I tolerated you.”



Agatha felt the pang in her chest. This wasn’t new, her mother’s rejection of her, but living without it for the last ten years helped heal that part of her. 



Her mother walked up towards the door of the basement, turning around one last time before leaving.



“Let’s see how obedient you are tomorrow. Sweet dreams, my dear.” She bolted the door behind her and Agatha slumped into the sofa below her. Her tears finally caught up with her and she sobbed into her hands. How did she get in this mess, and how the hell will she get out of it?

The Great Escape

Chapter Summary

Y'all, I probably rewrote this 15 times... Turns out, it's much harder to escape on paper than it is on the movies... Oh well, have at it! We're almost through the worst of it.

Chapter Notes

TW: Violence, but I’ll hold your hand through it.

Agatha’s POV



Agatha woke up on the uncomfortable sofa with an ache in her neck from being bundled up to keep warm. Sometime during the night it started snowing and the one musty blanket they threw down at her last night was barely enough to keep her from freezing. Agatha also needed to pee, like badly and she was not going to use the bucket they gave her. She might be a hostage, but she still had her fucking standards.



Trying her luck one last time, Agatha pulled the blanket around her shoulders and shuffled to the small window in the basement, pushing and pulling to see if it had any budge at all, but nothing, the only thing she felt was the cold from the thin sheen of snow coating the window sill. 

 

Another look at the bent bucket in the corner made her stomach turn, but it also gave her an idea. She dropped the blanket where she stood and climbed up the stairs to the door of the basement, and started banging on the door for them to open. If her plan had any chance of working, it was worth a chance, she thought before slamming her fists on the wood again.



“Hey!” she yelled, “I need the bathroom you assholes!” 



Nothing. She tried again. “Please!” she pleaded dramatically. 



Eventually, after increasing the force and intensity of her banging on the door, it creaked opened.



“What do you want?” the scruffy voiced man grumbled through a small crack in the door.



Agatha hoped with all her might that this dumbass would fall for her antics.



“Please… sir.” she asked, batting her eyes in exaggeration. “I really need to use the bathroom. The real one. Don’t get me wrong, I love and appreciate the bucket, but it’s not really ideal for… lady things.” 



The man’s eyes widened in panic as he realized what she meant. Got him, she thought. It was the 21th century and men still panicked at the mention of a fucking period. 



“If I promise to behave, can I please use the bathroom in the house?” Agatha pleaded with a big, bright, fake smile.



He looked around for a moment, the doubt in his demeanor evident, but after another pained expression from Agatha while she awkwardly pointed to her uterus, he finally agreed.



“Fine, but no funny business.” he grumbled.



The door closed and Agatha heard the chain lock release from the other side of the door and it opened. 



She held her hands up, “No funny business, I just need the bathroom.” 



The man grabbed her hands and held it behind her back as he walked her over to the bathroom. Agatha took the opportunity to see where she was. The house smelled funny, but it was empty, except for the two of them it seemed. The decor looked plain, more old brown and beige furniture, no pictures against the walls, temporary. This wasn’t someone’s house, this was a base, a temporary place to crash while on a job.



“Here,” he said, pushing her inside. “Don’t try anything and be quick. The boss lady is on her way and I am not getting the whip over a tampon.”



Agatha smiled after straightening herself, as she stumbled forward, almost hitting the sink. When the door was closed she used the toilet while taking in her surroundings and the contents of the bathroom.



A small window with bars too narrow to climb out of. A bar of soap she would not be touching. A dirty towel hanging over the shower door. A mop. Bingo.



Agatha quietly got up from the toilet after finishing up and took the mop, seeing if she could break it somehow. After trying to break it over her knee like she’s seen in the movies and failing horribly, she hooked the one end of the mop behind the pedestal of the sink and pulled the stick back like a big lever. Finally a crack and when it broke, she fell backwards against the door. “Fuck.” she whispered, rubbing her elbow where she hit the door.



“Hey!” the man yelled, “What’s going on in there.”



“Just cleaning up. I slipped.” she barked. Looking down on the floor the broken mop stick made a decent weapon for now. It was more than she counted on finding anyway and the break in the middle of the stick had a nice sharp edge. She grabbed it and held it tightly behind her back as she stood up to get ready for the door to open. “I’m done.” she sang, too cheery to be believable.



Agatha took a deep breath and the moment the door creaked open, she swung the stick at the man’s head, hitting him on the side of his ear. He stumbled backwards and grabbed at his head. “Fucking bitch!” he moaned.



Agatha pushed him out of the way and started running to where she remembered the living room to be, but the unfamiliar layout of the house let man catch up with her. He caught the back of her shirt and tackled her to the ground with a hard thump.



Agatha felt her breath get forced out of her chest as they fell to the ground. She struggled to get free and her stick fell to the side of her, just too far away to reach. The man was straddling her and holding her down while she flung her arms to hit him or to push him off of her. With a particularly strong swing of her arm, she hit him in the nose, hearing a soft crack. 



She felt the pain sparking through her hand, but quickly deduced that it wasn’t from the bones in her hand cracking against his face, but from the punch cracking the cartilage in his nose as the blood started dripping from his face onto the front of her shirt. He cried in pain and lifted himself off of her slightly, allowing her to wiggle herself loose a bit more, just enough for her to be able to reach the end of her makeshift weapon. 



Not wasting any more time, she tried to whack him with the stick again, this time with the sharper side of the stick. He was fighting back, but Agatha had enough. In that moment, she wasn’t just fighting to be free from under his weight, she was fighting for her son, for Rio. To see them again and to be able to hold them again. With added determination, she stuck it as hard as she could one final time, pegging the sharp end of the stick into the meat of his leg.



A loud cry echoed through the house as he fell over to the side holding onto his leg as the blood started gushing out of the wound. Agatha scrambled to get up, stepping as far away from him as she could. She had to get away now. She scanned the room quickly, looking for something to use as another weapon, in case he got up again. On the kitchen counter she saw a small pocket knife and ran to grab it, opening it up as soon as she put her hands on it. 



She turned to run to the front door and saw the man pushing himself up off the floor. “Back the fuck off!” she yelled at him, holding the pocket knife up in front of her as he stumbled towards her, the stick still protruding from his thigh. 



“You’ll pay for this, you bitch,” he said, launching himself at her, but his foot caught on the chair next to him and he fell face first against the kitchen cabinets, falling to the floor with a loud thud. He didn’t move. Agatha laughed in disbelief as she carefully kicked his body to see if he was awake but he seemed to be out cold, or dead, she didn’t mind either and wasted no more time to run to the front door of the house to get the hell out of there. 



She opened the door and immediately felt the cold air cut through her. For a moment she thought to just make a run for it in the cold, but she knew she wouldn’t make it far in the pajamas she was wearing. Her eye caught a jacket hanging over a chair and she ran back to grab it. She pulled it on and bolted out of the door. 



As soon as the cold hit her in the face she stood still in her tracks, taking a deep breath. She wasn’t free yet, but this felt close. She just had to figure out where she was and how she would get back to her family. Agatha ran down the steps of the porch, her slippers were falling off her feet, but she simply pulled them back on and hit the road. 



When she neared the end of the short driveway to the road, she saw a car approach in the distance. The car was definitely heading her way, she had to hide and fucking fast incase it was the boss lady, Evanora coming back for another round of verbal torture. Who knew what she was capable of these days, and now that Agatha was trying to escape, she will definitely be furious. 



Agatha huddled behind a bunch of barrels just off the road in time to hear the car pull into the driveway of the house she escaped from. She could peek through a small opening between two of the barrels and her suspicions were confirmed. Evanora and two other men she couldn’t yet recognize. 



A man in a long black coat followed behind Evanora as she walked up to the house while the driver of the car leaned on the side of the car, lighting a cigarette. Evanora stopped when she saw the door standing ajar, and turned to say something to the man behind her. He turned and Agatha ducked back down to hide, but not before she saw his face, it was Ralph fucking Bohner.



Fuck. Agatha’s heart thumped in her chest, she had to get away and now was her only chance. If Ralph found her, he’d kill her, she was sure of it. Agatha squeezed her eyes shut, she had to be brave, she had to survive this. 



Agatha was freezing, only wearing the stolen jacket over her pajamas and her flimsy slippers to cover her feet. They would soon discover the injured guy inside the house and the empty basement, but she couldn’t risk running down the road with the guy leaning against the car, that would definitely be too obvious, she would be a sitting, or running duck, and she has never really been the athletic type.



Agatha hunched back down to figure out a plan. The driver probably had the keys to the car in his pockets or if she was lucky they’d still be in the car’s ignition. Agatha held onto the small pocket knife she forgot she took from the kitchen and looked through the barrels, scanning the area again. 



Just then she heard the front door of the house swing open. “Where the hell did she go?” Evanora yelled at the driver. “Find her and bring her back. Now!”



The driver flicked his cigarette to the side as Agatha peeked through the barrels, watching Evanora storm off back into the house. The driver started to look for her around the side of the house. It would only be a matter of time before he found her where she was hiding. She looked down at the small pocket knife. It will have to do , she thought.



Agatha watched the driver of the car disappear around the corner of the house and ran to the driver’s side of the car. It was locked, no keys in sight. She heard the man shuffle somewhere close to her and hurried to hide behind the car. The driver returned back towards the car, walking slowly, kicking the dirt in boredom as he walked, obviously not the most enthusiastic goon Evanora could have hired.



He stopped next to the car to light up another cigarette. Agatha could smell the smoky sweat coming from his coat from how close she was to him. It was now or never. She held her breath as he looked around superficially. Agatha opened the small pocket knife in her hands. She’s only seen this move in movies, where the person’s heel would be sliced to incapacitate them. Would that even work, like where should she cut? 



No, she wasn’t some trained fucking secret agent, but she was desperate enough. Not thinking about it too much, she jumped up and plunged the knife into the side of the man’s neck. He turned to her with wide eyes and grabbed at his neck while he stumbled backwards. Agatha froze in place as she watched him fall onto his back, bleeding out. She probably killed him. Fuck. 



“ Two down …” her inappropriately timed thoughts whispered. This wasn’t time to think of her headcount now. Agatha spared no more time and ran towards the body, digging though his pockets for the keys to the car. She patted him down as quickly as possible while keeping an eye on the front door and the side of the house. She couldn’t take the chance of Evanora or Ralph spotting her. She wouldn’t be captured again.



The deep side pocket of his coat revealed a set of keys with a smiling devil emoji keychain. “Fitting, mother.” she mumbled to herself and pressed the key remote to unlock the car. 



Just as she was about to fumble the key into the ignition, Evanora and Ralph burst through the front door. Agatha locked eyes with her mother as Ralph started running to the car. 



“Fucking start !” Agatha yelled as she turned the key. Ralph tried to pull the door open but it was locked luckily and on the third turn of the key the car finally started just as he started banging against the window to break it.



Without any more hesitation or even a look in the rear view mirror Agatha slammed her foot on the pedal and pulled off in reverse, hitting the barrels that kept her hidden earlier. She lost her fucks a while ago, “Not my car, not my problem.” Agatha laughed as she sped away, leaving a cloud of dust in her rearview mirror. 



Agatha stole a quick look behind her watching as Ralph ran out into the street behind her. She finally got away, now she only needed to find out where the hell she was and how she was getting home to her family.



Rio’s POV



It has now been almost one day, 15 hours and 53 minutes since Agatha was kidnapped from the safe house. In Rio’s mind, it has probably been one day, 15 hours and 48 minutes since she was too late to stop the kidnappers from getting away with the love of her life. She still hated herself for not being able to stop them from dragging and shoving Agatha’s limp body into the back of the black van they came in.



To make matters even worse, the news footage of the live stream replayed on each and every screen in the house it seemed, taunting her and reminding her of the fact that she may have lost her. Every time she watched it replay on the news it ended the same, no matter how hard she wished for another ending, it always ended with Agatha smiling and obviously crying, yelling into the camera only to disappear as the screen blacked-out. 



Rio tried very hard to not imagine what would happen to Agatha after the black out, after the camera was turned off. Agatha obviously didn’t follow her captor's orders, she’s Agatha, when would she ever, but what consequences did that stunt mean for her? Would they hurt her? Kill her? 



Evanora was Agatha’s mother, sure, but the more Rio learned about the woman, the more she realized that the woman was a mother in title only. A real mother wouldn’t put her own daughter through what she has put Agatha through. No real mother would be the spearhead of her own daughter’s capture and torture to help get a murderer’s charges dropped. No real mother would give her own daughter over to her killers for money.



Conclusion, Evanora wasn’t a real mother, she was a monster. A monster Rio hoped would be found and arrested and shoved into the deepest, darkest prison cells there was, before Rio could put her own hands on the woman. But really, Rio’s only hope was that they actually find Agatha and bring her back. The waiting was killing her and she could see the worry in all her friends’ faces.



“Please Alice,” Rio sighed, dropping into the chair next to Alice where the agent was typing away on her laptop, “Tell me you guys are getting somewhere?”



“I can’t tell you everything yet, but we may have located a house a few towns over that belonged to a relative of Evanora. We’re confirming the details for the warrant to search the property.” Alice answered in a hushed voice. “But Rio, you need to keep this to yourself. I’m not allowed to tell you anything about the case.”



“Who am I going to tell? I just want you guys to find her.” Rio pleaded. “How long does a warrant take?”



“We’ll probably get it by the end of the day. I’ve got the guys on standby at the station to head out there as soon as we can.” Alice whispered.



Just then Alice’s phone rang and she got up to answer it away from Rio. Rio was left alone with Alice’s laptop and realized her opportunity. How long will Agatha be safe before the warrant is issued to search the house? Rio looked to see Alice still talking on her phone with her back turned to Rio, and Rio scrolled through Alice’s emails. She searched around and saw the location of the house. Bingo.



Rio took a photo of the laptop screen and hid her phone in her pocket as she got up and bolted out of the room to the living room where she remembered she saw Lilia’s car keys hanging on the key hooks on the wall. Everyone was too distracted to notice, so Rio grabbed the keys off the hook on the wall and snuck out to the garage. Inside the garage, Rio grabbed a crowbar from the racks on the side of the walls. She wasn’t good with a gun, but swinging a heavy metal rod at Ralph or Evanora sounded more doable. Rio pressed the button on the car keys and Lilia’s silver Mercedes came to life as the lights flickered.



Rio climbed into the driver’s side and quickly entered the address she found on Alice’s laptop into her navigation app on her phone. The location was on a remote piece of land about two hours from Lilia’s safehouse. If the police got to Agatha first, she’d be right on their tails, but she was done waiting around. 



“I’m coming, my love.” Rio said, more to herself, but she hoped Agatha could feel her coming. Rio sped down the stone driveway and turned onto the main road, determined to save the woman her whole heart belonged to.

To be Found

Chapter Summary

We’re jumping between POV’s a bit because things are happening like this *snaps fingers twice*

Chapter Notes

TW: Violence and action, but we’ll be okay, promise.

See the end of the chapter for more notes

Rio’s POV



Rio grunted in frustration as she gripped the steering wheel tight, no matter how fast she tried to drive, she still felt she wasn’t getting to Agatha fast enough. She was already pushing the car well past the speed limit, just enough to still be able to have decent control over Lilia’s car. It wouldn’t be in anyone’s interest if she crashed on her way to try and save Agatha, now would it. 



What also didn’t help her building frustration was her fucking phone that kept on ringing and ringing. She knew exactly who it was but she hadn’t cared to answer out of pure spite. Alice and her team wasn’t getting anywhere and Rio decided to take matters into her own hands. After rejecting all four of Alice’s previous calls, Rio finally gave in and answered reluctantly.



“What, Alice?” Rio spat into the car speakers.



“Rio, what the fuck…” Alice yelled through the phone. Rio rolled her eyes. Seriously. Did they really think she would just sit around and wait for better days?



“Alice…” Rio tried, sighing. There was no way Alice would be able to convince her to turn the car around. Not unless, by some miracle, they had Agatha safe at home before she could find her herself.



“Please don’t be a fucking dumbass about this, Rio. You’re going to get yourself killed or hurt and Agatha…”



“That’s why I am doing this Alice, for Agatha. I’m sick and tired of sitting around and hearing the same excuses over and over, that you’ll find her, that you’re so close. I know where she is and unlike you and your suits , I don’t have to wait around for a fucking warrant before I can actually do something.” Rio yelled back. Rio rubbed at her temple as she leaned against the window.



“Rio, you know no one can keep you or Agatha safe if you do this. Please, just come back to the safehouse and…”



“And what, Alice? You’ll wait for the judge or the rescue team? I’m already a half an hour away from her, and where are your guys, huh? Still waiting for the thumbs up? Still waiting for their lift to pick them up? I’m done waiting, Alice. Agatha is done waiting to be saved.” Rio asked, trying her hardest not to actually scream into the car speakers.



“Rio…” Alice tried to reason with her but it fell on deaf ears.



“I said I’m done waiting, Alice. She’s…” Rio felt the tears starting to pool in her eyes. “I love her.” Rio said quietly. Fuck, she had to keep it together if she was going to be any use to Agatha.



The line went silent for a few seconds. Rio heard the cops in the background of Alice’s call murmuring in the silence.



Alice sighed audibly into the phone, “Urgh, just… Just don’t do anything fucking stupid. Wait for us if you can, we just got the order to go ahead and our team is right behind you. Please Rio… we all care about her.” Alice sounded defeated, but Rio heard the earnest concern in Alice’s voice. 



She quickly squeezed her eyes shut and felt a tear roll down the side of her cheek. “I’m not letting her… or myself get hurt, I promise Alice… but I’m getting her out of there with or without you.” Rio said finally.



“Just be safe and… good luck Rio.” Alice said with a sigh, ending the call.



Rio threw her phone to the side and it hopped off the passenger seat and dropped to the floor of the car. She’ll worry about that later. She was being reckless and stupid, she knew this. She had no training in any physical combat, apart from the one time she almost broke her wrist on the punching bag at gym. She only had a fucking crowbar, a GPS location and all the love in her heart to save Agatha, it will have to be enough this time.



The sun setting low in the sky was annoying Rio the most. Not only was it shining in her eyes, she obviously didn’t have her sunglasses with her, but it was also reminding her of another hour that passed with Agatha still not safe in her arms.



What also added to her annoyance was the fact that she had to stop for fucking gas and that was a very fucking inconvenient red light flickering on the dashboard. What kind of safehouse doesn’t keep their car’s tank full? Rio sniffed a laugh at herself and her inner dialogue, as if she would know what the protocol of a practical and functioning safe house would be, but a loaded gun in the cubby and a full tank of gas sounded like good practice in general.



Far on the horizon, Rio spotted the lights for the gas station. The road felt too abandoned and she thanked the stars appearing in the darkening sky that it at least had a gas station on her way. Running out of gas on the way or on the run would fucking suck. 



Rio pulled off the road and into the gas station, parking Lilia’s car in front of one of the gas pumps. These weren’t the self service pumps that she was used to, so she turned off the car and got out, waiting for the attendant to approach her. 



“Ma’am?” the man dressed in a thick branded jacket spoke.



“Hi,” Rio greeted, she opened her wallet and took out a $50 bill and handed it to the attendant who started filling up the fuel tank.



“Where are you heading?” he asked her.



“Visiting a friend in the area.” she answered bluntly. This man didn’t need to know where she was going. He seemed uninterested in her answer anyway and continued filling up the fuel tank.



Rio felt the temperature dropping as the sun set further and shivered. She decided to rather wait in the car for the attendant to finish up.



“All done.” the man said from behind her and Rio thanked him as she started the car back up.



Rio started the car back up, and turned up the heating. The cold was really setting in now and she could feel her jacket wasn’t going to cut it any longer. She hoped Agatha was warm enough. 



She pulled out of the pump station and heard her phone buzz again. Glimpsing to the side where the phone was still lying on the floor, she saw Alice’s contact pop up again. She was just out of reach of the phone and stopped the car just before she turned out onto the road again to bend down to reach the phone to answer. 



Rio stretched and finally reached the phone but before she could answer it, it dropped out of her hand when she felt the car shake as something hit it with a loud bang.



Agatha’s POV



A blur of winter colors whizzed past Agatha as she fled her capturers. She found herself laughing, almost hysterically as she wiped the tears from her face, speeding down the single lane road towards… fucking somewhere. The road felt endless and didn’t have much traffic and almost no signage to give her any idea where she was or where she was heading. She only knew she had to get away from Ralph and Evanora as quickly and far as possible. 



Agatha kept her eyes on the road, turning and straining her neck every now and then in search of any road sign, anything to tell her where the hell she was going. Her only clue was a sign saying that there was a gas stop a few miles ahead. She had no intention of stopping though, but maybe someone could help her with directions at least. 



The traffic on the road was quiet with only one or two cars passing her in the last hour, so she deduced that wherever this road led, no one else seemed to be heading the same way. She had to assume that Ralph and Evanora would find a way to catch up with her eventually. Their plan had flopped and she was their liability now. They were most likely fucking pissed at her.



The black van she was kidnapped in and hauled away was still parked in the driveway when she sped off in one of the goon’s cars. Now that she thought of it, she wished she could have tried to slash a tire on the van or something to slow them down even more, but that wasn’t high on her list of priorities in the heat of the moment. 



Agatha shrugged internally. Whatever. She has managed to get away for now and she would be lucky if they didn’t follow her. It has been an hour and she hasn’t seen any sign of them in her rearview mirrors, but she couldn’t slow down or stop now, not until she knew she was somewhere safe. It would also be dark soon, the sun was already hanging low over the horizon to her left, meaning she was heading somewhere north, but was she going north away from Westview or north towards Westview, that was the fucking question.



Agatha passed another sign for the gas station, getting closer to civilization with every minute. In the darkening horizon she saw the gas station and what looked like some car headlights and faint lights spilling from the gas station’s office. She slacked down as she approached.



If she was lucky enough, she’ll have enough time to stop at the gas station to get some directions and to call Alice or Rio to let them know where she was. 



But Agatha has never really been a lucky person or someone who believed in luck up until Rio showing up at Tony’s on a random Friday night. A life spent under Evanora’s thumb would do that to you, take away all hope of luck or happy endings. That’s why Agatha always worked twice as hard as those around her, because good things and happiness was never something that just happened for her, she had to work for it and earn it.



She had to admit that she was lucky with some things. Meeting Rio was one of them and of course having Nicky and not to mention her friends and chosen family. Ok she was more lucky than others, but getting kidnapped and held hostage by your own mother didn’t seem lucky at all. 



What also didn’t feel lucky was the pain in her forehead and the small drip of blood coming from her nose as she lifted herself off the steering wheel of her getaway car. 



She slowly pushed herself up and blinked to take in her surroundings. The front of the car was wrecked where the car’s hood was bent and lifted over the windscreen blocking her view. The only thing she saw of the object she hit was the flickering tail lights of another car.



“Fucking shit.” Agatha moaned as she felt her head throb.



She forced the door open and stumbled out of the car, nearly falling to the ground in her disorientation. When she was able to stabilize herself she turned to the car she hit. She couldn’t see the driver from where she stood and stumbled forward to see inside the car.



Draped over the passenger seat laid a woman, seemingly unconscious. Oh fuck, not another one.



“Hey! Hey! Help! Please help!” Agatha yelled to the gas station attendant who came running over towards them.



“I’ve already called 911. They’re on their way, ma’am.” he said as he started to work on getting the car door open.



“Oh my god, is she… is she okay?” Agatha asked worriedly as the burly man tried to open the woman’s door. When it finally opened, the man carefully lifted and pulled the woman out. Agatha’s eyes were filled with tears and she sobbed loudly as she spun around, she couldn’t look, “Oh god,” she cried. 



The man carefully put the woman down on the ground. “She’s okay.” he said, “She’s breathing fine.” Agatha turned back immediately, relief falling over her, but the second she got a good look at the woman in question her own legs gave way almost instantly as she met the eyes of the woman laying on the ground.



“Oh my go… RIO! ” Agatha yelled as she recognized her. How can this be?



“Agatha?” Rio croaked blinking her eyes open in disbelief. “Agatha!” Rio called as she sprang upright, ignoring any pain in her body and moved with lightning speed to reach Agatha.



“I can’t believe it…” Agatha cried against Rio’s shoulder as Rio wrapped her arms around her. “How are you here? How is this…”



“Agatha, I’m here. I’ve got you. I’m here.” Rio answered frantically as she held Agatha close to her.



Rio held onto her so tightly, Agatha could feel her heart beat against her chest. Rio was feeling her everywhere, confirming her actually being here and alive and in her arms.



Agatha grabbed Rio’s wrists and held her teary gaze. Complete relief and disbelief filled her. She was at a total loss for words. Of all the people, of all the places and times, she managed to not only crash into someone while trying to escape her own kidnapping, no she actually crashed into Rio. The gods must be crazy.



“I almost killed you.” Agatha laughed, slamming her fist into Rio’s shoulder. Her tears were now flowing freely as they finally held onto each other again. 



“Ow!” Rio flinched. “You ran into me, remember?”



“Fuck sorry,” Agatha smiled.



Agatha felt Rio cup her cheek and for a moment everything around them faded away. The cold snowy ground they were hunched on. The flickering lights of the two smashed cars. The gas station attendant. The faint siren of the ambulance approaching. The possibility of Evanora and Ralph showing up. It was just them.



Agatha leaned in to press a wet, teary kiss to Rio’s lips. “What are you doing here?” she asked Rio. Agatha tucked a piece of Rio’s fringe behind her ear. A bruise was forming on her forehead. Agatha’s thumb traced over it carefully.



“What am I…? Agatha, I came to find you.” Rio adjusted herself a bit to sit upright. Agatha never let go of her hand, holding onto her with everything she had left. “Alice found the address of Evanora’s hideaway house, I stole it, stole Lilia’s car…” 



Both of them looked at the wreck of the two cars next to them. Lilia would understand.



“I couldn’t sit around and wait for another cop or detective to tell me “ We’re close” or “We need a warrant” so I thought fuck that. I’m not letting them lose you, because I can’t lose you. Not again.” Rio’s smile was pained and her tears streamed down her cheeks. Agatha’s heart felt like it was bursting at the sight.



Agatha couldn’t find any words other than “I fucking love you.” She cupped Rio’s neck and brought her face closer to kiss her with all the love in her heart. “You found me.”



The quiet gas station suddenly felt very crowded as the ambulance and two police vehicles pulled up to the scene. Agatha helped Rio up and Rio’s arms wrapped around Agatha’s cold body. 



“You’re freezing.” Rio said, rubbing Agatha’s sides.



“Remind me to wear something more appropriate when I get kidnapped next time.” Agatha smirked.



“I even missed your smart ass mouth.” Rio laughed quietly. 



A police woman approached them followed by the two EMT’s.



“You ladies doin’ okay?” the officer asked. “Let’s get you checked out while I take your statements.”



Agatha felt uneasy leaving Rio’s side, but she followed the EMT to the ambulance to see to her head wounds. Agatha watched Rio from the back of the ambulance as she spoke to the police officer. Agatha had a lot to explain to the officers, but Rio convinced the officers to call Alice to confirm their elaborate story of Agatha’s kidnapping and eventual escape.



“We need to get you checked out as well ma’am.” The EMT said to Rio as she returned to Agatha in the ambulance.



“Uh, yeah sure.” Rio frowned. “Can I have a second alone with her please?” she asked the EMT, who nodded and walked off to the side to give them some privacy.



Agatha’s eyes closed at the touch of Rio’s hand against her bandages on her head. “You okay?” Rio asked her quietly.



“Yeah, I just want to get home.” Agatha sighed.



“The officer called Alice.” Rio said, throwing her thumb over her shoulder. “We should wait here, but they’ve got a team going to the house where they held you and she’s coming with Lilia to pick us up.”



“Rio I…” Agatha dropped her head. A dull pain spread across her skull as she started to feel the full impact of the crash. “I kill…”



“Shhh,” Rio said, pulling her into a hug. “Let’s have Alice and Lilia deal with that.” Rio kissed her forehead and cupped her cheek again. “What’s important now is to get you warm and to get you back to Nicky.”



“He’s probably worried sick.” Agatha’s heart ached for what her poor son had to go through. 



“He was so brave through it all, but I know he’ll be so happy to see you again.” Rio smiled at her warmly and Agatha couldn’t help but feel the relief settle over her that her son had Rio to comfort him through this ordeal.



“Thank you Rio.” Agatha whispered. “For finding me. For being here…”



“I know my love.” Rio smiled, kissing her softly. 



Agatha’s whole body relaxed under Rio’s lips and in her embrace. Finally, she felt safe again.   



“Where the fuck are we?” Agatha asked, laughing with Rio at the absurdity of it all.
